****** Code
#+BEGIN_SRC c :tangle usb/usbreset.c
/* usbreset -- send a USB port reset to a USB device */
#include <stdio.h>
#include <unistd.h>
#include <fcntl.h>
#include <errno.h>

#include <sys/ioctl.h>

#include <linux/usbdevice_fs.h>


int main(int argc, char **argv)
{
	const char *filename;
	int fd;
	int rc;

	if (argc != 2) {
		fprintf(stderr, "Usage: usbreset device-filename\n");
		return 1;
	}
	filename = argv[1];

	fd = open(filename, O_WRONLY);
	if (fd < 0) {
		perror("Error opening output file");
		return 1;
	}

	printf("Resetting USB device %s\n", filename);
	rc = ioctl(fd, USBDEVFS_RESET, 0);
	if (rc < 0) {
		perror("Error in ioctl");
		return 1;
	}
	printf("Reset successful\n");

	close(fd);
	return 0;
}
#+END_SRC
****** Compile
#+BEGIN_SRC sh :dir usb
gcc -o usbreset usbreset.c -lusb
#+END_SRC

#+RESULTS:

***** Code 2
To compile use: gcc -o outputname resetusb.c -lusb
#+BEGIN_SRC c
#include <stdio.h>
#include <usb.h>

int main(void)
{
      struct usb_bus *busses;
      usb_init();
      usb_find_busses();
      usb_find_devices();
      busses = usb_get_busses();
      struct usb_bus *bus;
      int c, i, a;
      /* ... */
      for (bus = busses; bus; bus = bus->next) {
        struct usb_device *dev;
        int val;
        usb_dev_handle *junk;
        for (dev = bus->devices; dev; dev = dev->next) {
          char buf[1024];
          junk = usb_open ( dev );
          usb_get_string_simple(junk,2,buf,1023);
          if ( junk == NULL ){
            printf("Can't open %p (%s)\n", dev, buf );
          } else {
            val = usb_reset(junk);
            printf( "reset %p %d (%s)\n", dev, val, buf );
          }
          usb_close(junk);
        }
      }
}
#+END_SRC


command: gcc -o outputname resetusb.c -lusb
***** Command
#+BEGIN_SRC sh
udevadm trigger --action=add
#+END_SRC

***** Kernel parameter
you have to enable the following within the kernel config
CONFIG_USB_EHCI_TT_NEWSCHED=y
*** USB 3G Modem
**** SMS
***** [[http://www.pcbackup.it/asterisk-chan-dongle-sms-memory-dongle-full/][ASTERISK CHAN DONGLE SMS MEMORY DONGLE FULL]]
using massivley our sms booster can happened to receive on asterisk CLI the sms memory full even if you have set the
autodeletesms=yes in [general] section of dongle.conf
Sometimes modem receive SMS and store in SIM storage.
So ‘+CMTI: “SM”,1′ reported by modem to chan_dongle.

But chan_dongle can use only “ME” (dongle) storage for read and delete messages, and do commands:
AT+CMGR=1 AT+CMGD=1 for “ME” (because issue AT+CPMS=”ME”,”ME”,”ME” at initialize time)

Both command shortly report OK,
but (second bug) OK in responce of AT+CMGR handled wrong and does’t trigger incoming_sms state back

causes two troubles

1) persistent “SMS” state

2) SM storage report ^SMMEMFULL when full

so i create a script according to http://wiki.e1550.mobi/doku.php?id=troubleshooting

to delete sms from both sim and dongle memory and plced it to /etc/cron.daily

like this:
#+BEGIN_SRC sh :dir /sudo::
asterisk -rx 'dongle cmd dongle0 AT+CPMS=\"SM\",\"SM\",\"SM\"'
sleep1
asterisk -rx 'dongle cmd dongle0 AT+CMGD=1,4'
sleep 1
asterisk -rx 'dongle cmd dongle0 AT+CPMS=\"ME\",\"ME\",\"ME\"'
sleep 1
asterisk -rx 'dongle cmd dongle0 AT+CMGD=1,4'
#+END_SRC

#+RESULTS:
| SM                   | SM                            | SM' Command queued for execute |
| [dongle0] 'AT+CMGD=1 | 4' Command queued for execute |                                |
| ME                   | ME                            | ME' Command queued for execute |
| [dongle0] 'AT+CMGD=1 | 4' Command queued for execute |                                |

**** [[http://www.anchor.com.au/blog/2010/02/ssh-controlmaster-the-good-the-bad-the-ugly/][SSH ControlMaster]]: The Good, The Bad, The Ugly
On some trivial benchmarking I did when validating ControlMaster for our use, I found that we were saving nearly 2.5 seconds per connection — a drop from 3.3 seconds to 0.8. Mighty convenient.
It’s simple to use, too.
If you just want to enable “opportunistic” multiplexing,

** Can I automatically add a new host to known_hosts?
*** Local User
using key-scan would be the right & unobtrusive way to do it.
#+NAME: addhost
#+BEGIN_SRC sh :var HOST="" :port cat()
ssh-keyscan -t rsa,dsa $HOST 2>&1 | sort -u - ~/.ssh/known_hosts > ~/.ssh/tmp_hosts
mv ~/.ssh/tmp_hosts ~/.ssh/known_hosts
#+END_SRC

#+RESULTS:

#+BEGIN_SRC elisp :var file="" :results raw
  (defun file-string(file)
  "Read The contents of a file and return as a string"
  (with-temp-buffer
    (insert-file-contents file)
    (buffer-string)))
  (file-string file)
#+END_SRC

* chrome shortcuts
*** [[http://www.getsidekick.com/blog/chrome-keyboard-shortcuts][25 shortcuts links]]
*** Manage Tabs
**** DONE [[http://www.shortcutworld.com/en/linux/Chrome.html][shortcutls.com]]
***** DONE Ctrl+TOpen new tab
***** DONE Ctrl+W/Ctrl+F4Close tab (or close Chrome if only one tab is open)
***** DONE Ctrl+Shift+TReopen last tab closed. Up to 10 tabs.
***** DONE Ctrl+1 through Ctrl+8Jump to first tab, second tab, etc.
***** DONE Ctrl+9Switch to the last tab
***** DONE Ctrl+Tab/Ctrl+Shift+TabSwitch to the next / previous tab
***** DONE (or use ctrl+page up/ctrl+page down)
***** DONE Ctrl+NOpen new Chrome window
***** DONE Ctrl+Shift+NOpen new Chrome window in incognito mode
***** DONE Alt+F4Close current window
***** DONE Ctrl and click on linkOpen link in a new background tab
***** DONE Shift+ctrl and click on linkOpen link in a new foreground tab
***** DONE Shift and click on linkOpen link in a new window
***** DONE Alt and click on linkDownload link
***** DONE Drag link to existing tabOpen link in selected tab
***** DONE Drag link to tab barOpen link in a new tab in the specified position on the tab

**** Address Bar
***** Alt+D/Ctrl+LJump to address bar; highlights current webpage URI if available
***** Ctrl+EEnter search query in address bar
***** Home/End in address barJump to beginning / end of address bar
***** Ctrl+a in address barSelect all text of address. Also use shift+end with cursor at beginning or shift+home with cursor at end
***** Type name of site and press Ctrl+EnterAdd www. to beginning and .com to end of input and opens the web address in current tab.
***** Type name of site and press Alt+EnterAdd www. to beginning and .com to end of input and opens the web address in new background tab.
***** Type search term and press EnterPerform a search using the search engine associated with the keyword or the URI.
* Arch Installation
** check partitions
#+BEGIN_SRC sh
lsblk
#+END_SRC
or
#+BEGIN_SRC sh
fdisk -l
#+END_SRC
** chreate parti
#+BEGIN_SRC sh
cfdisk /dev/sd*
#+END_SRC
** mount partitions
*** Primary
#+BEGIN_SRC sh
mkfs.ext4 /dev/sda1
mount /dev/sda1 /mnt
#+END_SRC
*** Swap
#+BEGIN_SRC sh
mkswap /dev/sdb1
swapon /dev/sdb1
#+END_SRC
** Installation
#+BEGIN_SRC sh
pacstrap /mnt base base-devel xorg xorg-server xorg-server-utils xorg-apps xorg-xinit xorg-message xscreensaver feh ttf-inconsolata xmonad xmonad-contrib ghc cabal-install xmobar haddock gmrun dmenu
#+END_SRC
* Virtual
** Virtual box in ubuntu
#+BEGIN_SRC
sudo sh -c "echo 'deb http://download.virtualbox.org/virtualbox/debian '$(lsb_release -cs)' contrib non-free' > /etc/apt/sources.list.d/virtualbox.list" && wget -q http://download.virtualbox.org/virtualbox/debian/oracle_vbox.asc -O- | sudo apt-key add - && sudo apt-get update && sudo apt-get install virtualbox-5.0
#+END_SRC
